<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++ notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// C++ has unusual iterator syntax!
vector&lt;string&gt; fruits = {&quot;apple&quot;, &quot;pear&quot;, ... };

for (auto it = fruits.begin(); it != fruits.end(); ++it)
  cout &lt;&lt; *it;"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> C++ has unusual iterator syntax!</span>
vector&lt;string&gt; fruits = {<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>apple<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>pear<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, ... };

<span class="pl-k">for</span> (<span class="pl-k">auto</span> it = fruits.begin(); it != fruits.end(); ++it)
  cout &lt;&lt; *it;</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">So how does looping work under the hood?</h3><a id="user-content-so-how-does-looping-work-under-the-hood" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: So how does looping work under the hood?" href="#so-how-does-looping-work-under-the-hood"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">When you loop over the items in an iterable object , the language secretly uses an iterator to move through the items! This is a fantastic example of Syntactic Sugar!</p>
<p dir="auto">When you do this:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-kotlin notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// Kotlin: iterate over list of #s
val numbers = listOf(10,20,30,42)

for (v in numbers) {
  println(v)
}"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Kotlin: iterate over list of #s</span>
<span class="pl-k">val</span> numbers <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">listOf</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>,<span class="pl-c1">20</span>,<span class="pl-c1">30</span>,<span class="pl-c1">42</span>)

<span class="pl-k">for</span> (v <span class="pl-k">in</span> numbers) {
  <span class="pl-c1">println</span>(v)
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Here's what's really happening (the language generates this code secretly for you):</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-kotlin notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="val numbers = listOf(10,20,30,42)

val it = numbers.iterator()
while (it.hasNext()) {
  val v = it.next()
  println(v)
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">val</span> numbers <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">listOf</span>(<span class="pl-c1">10</span>,<span class="pl-c1">20</span>,<span class="pl-c1">30</span>,<span class="pl-c1">42</span>)

<span class="pl-k">val</span> it <span class="pl-k">=</span> numbers.iterator()
<span class="pl-k">while</span> (it.hasNext()) {
  <span class="pl-k">val</span> v <span class="pl-k">=</span> it.next()
  <span class="pl-c1">println</span>(v)
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Or when you do this:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-swift notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// Swift: iterate over range

for v in 1...1000000 {
  print(v)
}"><pre><span class="pl-c">// Swift: iterate over range</span>

for <span class="pl-s1">v</span> in <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">...</span><span class="pl-c1">1000000</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-en">print</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span>v<span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Here's what's really happening:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-swift notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="var range = 1...1000000

var it = range.makeIterator()
while true {
  var v = it.next()
  if (v == nil) { break }
  print(v)
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">range</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-c1">...</span><span class="pl-c1">1000000</span>

<span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">it</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> range<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">makeIterator</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
while true <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-k">var</span> <span class="pl-s1">v</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> it<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">next</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
  if <span class="pl-kos">(</span>v <span class="pl-c1">==</span> <span class="pl-smi">nil</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span> break <span class="pl-kos">}</span>
  <span class="pl-en">print</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span>v<span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">How are iterators implemented?</h3><a id="user-content-how-are-iterators-implemented" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: How are iterators implemented?" href="#how-are-iterators-implemented"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">There are two primary approaches for creating iterators:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>With Traditional Classes: An iterator is an object, implemented using regular OOP classes.</li>
<li>"True Iterators" aka Generators: An iterator is implemented by using a special type of function called a generator.</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Iterators built using traditional classes</h4><a id="user-content-iterators-built-using-traditional-classes" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Iterators built using traditional classes" href="#iterators-built-using-traditional-classes"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Let's see an iterator that is built using a traditional class - Python makes it easy.</p>
<p dir="auto">First we must define an iterable class (e.g., like a vector class) which we can iterate over. To make a class iterable, we must define an __iter__() method that creates and returns an iterator object. The ListsOfStrings class is an <em>iterable</em> class - NOT an iterator.  If its __iter__ method is called, it will return an iterator that can be used to iterate over its items.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class ListOfStrings:
  def __init__(self):
    self.array = []

  def add(self,val):
    self.array.append(val)

  def __iter__(self):
    it = OurIterator(self.array)   // calling __iter__ returns a new OurIterator object
    return it"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">ListOfStrings</span>:
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">array</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> []

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">add</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>,<span class="pl-s1">val</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">array</span>.<span class="pl-en">append</span>(<span class="pl-s1">val</span>)

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__iter__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">it</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">OurIterator</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">array</span>)   <span class="pl-c1">//</span> <span class="pl-s1">calling</span> <span class="pl-s1">__iter__</span> <span class="pl-s1">returns</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-s1">new</span> <span class="pl-v">OurIterator</span> <span class="pl-s1">object</span>
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">it</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Second we can define our OurIterator class. Notice that this iterator class is uniqely tied to our ListOfStrings class above. The two work hand-in-hand.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class OurIterator:
  def __init__(self, arr):
    self.arr = arr
    self.pos = 0

  def __next__(self):
    if self.pos &lt; len(self.arr):
      val = self.arr[self.pos]
      self.pos += 1
      return val
    else:
      raise StopIteration"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">OurIterator</span>:
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">arr</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">arr</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">arr</span>
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pos</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__next__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pos</span> <span class="pl-c1">&lt;</span> <span class="pl-en">len</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">arr</span>):
      <span class="pl-s1">val</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">arr</span>[<span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pos</span>]
      <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">pos</span> <span class="pl-c1">+=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>
      <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">val</span>
    <span class="pl-k">else</span>:
      <span class="pl-k">raise</span> <span class="pl-v">StopIteration</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Our iterator class must have a method called __next__() that gets the value of the item pointed to by the iterator, advances the iterator, and returns the value. As you can see, if the iterator has run out of items to iterate over (ther are no more items in the iterable object), the iterator (in Python) will throw an exception to tell the user of the iterator that there are no more items left.</p>
<p dir="auto">If we define our iterable class and iterator classes this way, Python will give us first-class looping support over our iterable class!</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="nerds = ListOfStrings()
nerds.add(&quot;Carey&quot;)
nerds.add(&quot;David&quot;)
nerds.add(&quot;Paul&quot;)

for n in nerds: 
  print(n)"><pre><span class="pl-s1">nerds</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">ListOfStrings</span>()
<span class="pl-s1">nerds</span>.<span class="pl-en">add</span>(<span class="pl-s">"Carey"</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">nerds</span>.<span class="pl-en">add</span>(<span class="pl-s">"David"</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">nerds</span>.<span class="pl-en">add</span>(<span class="pl-s">"Paul"</span>)

<span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">n</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-s1">nerds</span>: 
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">n</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">And here''s an example of an iterator in Java:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-java notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="import java.util.Iterator;  

class ListOfStrings implements Iterable&lt;String&gt; {
  private String[] array;
  private int numItems = 0, maxSize = 100;

  public ListOfStrings() 
    { array = new String[maxSize]; }
  public void add(String val) 
    { array[numItems++] = val; }
  @Override public Iterator&lt;String&gt; iterator() {      
    Iterator&lt;String&gt; it = new OurIterator();
    return it;
  }

  class OurIterator implements Iterator&lt;String&gt; {
    private int iteratorIndex = 0;
    @Override public boolean hasNext() 
      { return iteratorIndex &lt; numItems; }
    @Override public String next() 
      { return array[iteratorIndex++]; }
  }
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">import</span> <span class="pl-s1">java</span>.<span class="pl-s1">util</span>.<span class="pl-s1">Iterator</span>;  

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-smi">ListOfStrings</span> <span class="pl-k">implements</span> <span class="pl-smi">Iterable</span>&lt;<span class="pl-smi">String</span>&gt; {
  <span class="pl-k">private</span> <span class="pl-smi">String</span>[] <span class="pl-s1">array</span>;
  <span class="pl-k">private</span> <span class="pl-smi">int</span> <span class="pl-s1">numItems</span> = <span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-s1">maxSize</span> = <span class="pl-c1">100</span>;

  <span class="pl-k">public</span> <span class="pl-smi">ListOfStrings</span>() 
    { <span class="pl-s1">array</span> = <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-smi">String</span>[<span class="pl-s1">maxSize</span>]; }
  <span class="pl-k">public</span> <span class="pl-smi">void</span> <span class="pl-en">add</span>(<span class="pl-smi">String</span> <span class="pl-s1">val</span>) 
    { <span class="pl-s1">array</span>[<span class="pl-s1">numItems</span>++] = <span class="pl-s1">val</span>; }
  <span class="pl-c1">@</span><span class="pl-c1">Override</span> <span class="pl-k">public</span> <span class="pl-smi">Iterator</span>&lt;<span class="pl-smi">String</span>&gt; <span class="pl-en">iterator</span>() {      
    <span class="pl-smi">Iterator</span>&lt;<span class="pl-smi">String</span>&gt; <span class="pl-s1">it</span> = <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-smi">OurIterator</span>();
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">it</span>;
  }

  <span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-smi">OurIterator</span> <span class="pl-k">implements</span> <span class="pl-smi">Iterator</span>&lt;<span class="pl-smi">String</span>&gt; {
    <span class="pl-k">private</span> <span class="pl-smi">int</span> <span class="pl-s1">iteratorIndex</span> = <span class="pl-c1">0</span>;
    <span class="pl-c1">@</span><span class="pl-c1">Override</span> <span class="pl-k">public</span> <span class="pl-smi">boolean</span> <span class="pl-en">hasNext</span>() 
      { <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">iteratorIndex</span> &lt; <span class="pl-s1">numItems</span>; }
    <span class="pl-c1">@</span><span class="pl-c1">Override</span> <span class="pl-k">public</span> <span class="pl-smi">String</span> <span class="pl-en">next</span>() 
      { <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">array</span>[<span class="pl-s1">iteratorIndex</span>++]; }
  }
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Things to note:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>The ListOfStrings class implements Java's Iterable interface, which makes this clas an Iterable class (it can have its items iterated over). The class must then implement the iterator() method which can be used to obtain an iterator into the iterable object.</li>
<li>The Iterator class is a nested class within ListOfStrings, which lets it access the memer variables of ListOfStrings.  Notice how it implements the Iterator interface. To do so, it must provide a hasNext() method and a next() method.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">And here's how we'd use our class.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-java notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="public void testOurList() {         
  ListOfStrings nerds = 
    new ListOfStrings();

  nerds.add(&quot;Carey&quot;);
  nerds.add(&quot;David&quot;);
  nerds.add(&quot;Paul&quot;);

  Iterator it = nerds.iterator();  
  while (it.hasNext()) { 
    String value = (String)it.next();    
    System.out.println(value);
  } 

  for (String s: nerds)
    System.out.println(s);
}"><pre><span class="pl-k">public</span> <span class="pl-smi">void</span> <span class="pl-s1">testOurList</span>() {         
  <span class="pl-smi">ListOfStrings</span> <span class="pl-s1">nerds</span> = 
    <span class="pl-k">new</span> <span class="pl-smi">ListOfStrings</span>();

  <span class="pl-s1">nerds</span>.<span class="pl-en">add</span>(<span class="pl-s">"Carey"</span>);
  <span class="pl-s1">nerds</span>.<span class="pl-en">add</span>(<span class="pl-s">"David"</span>);
  <span class="pl-s1">nerds</span>.<span class="pl-en">add</span>(<span class="pl-s">"Paul"</span>);

  <span class="pl-smi">Iterator</span> <span class="pl-s1">it</span> = <span class="pl-s1">nerds</span>.<span class="pl-en">iterator</span>();  
  <span class="pl-k">while</span> (<span class="pl-s1">it</span>.<span class="pl-en">hasNext</span>()) { 
    <span class="pl-smi">String</span> <span class="pl-s1">value</span> = (<span class="pl-smi">String</span>)<span class="pl-s1">it</span>.<span class="pl-en">next</span>();    
    <span class="pl-smi">System</span>.<span class="pl-s1">out</span>.<span class="pl-en">println</span>(<span class="pl-s1">value</span>);
  } 

  <span class="pl-k">for</span> (<span class="pl-smi">String</span> <span class="pl-s1">s</span>: <span class="pl-s1">nerds</span>)
    <span class="pl-smi">System</span>.<span class="pl-s1">out</span>.<span class="pl-en">println</span>(<span class="pl-s1">s</span>);
}</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Notice how above we can manually get the iterator then use hasNext() and next() with it. Or we can use Java's looping syntax, and Java will use syntactic sugar, hiding the calls to get the iterator and use hasNext() and next().</p>
<p dir="auto">Ok, next let's see how to create a range() iterable using a class like we have in python (and many other languages):</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class OurIter:  # iterator class
  def __init__(self, start, end):
   self.cur = start
   self.end = end

  def __next__(self):
    if self.cur &lt; self.end:
      val = self.cur
      self.cur += 1
      return val
    else:
      raise StopIteration()

class OurRange:  # iterable class
  def __init__(self, end):
    self.end = end

  def __iter__(self):
    iter = OurIter(0, self.end)
    return iter"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">OurIter</span>:  <span class="pl-c"># iterator class</span>
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">start</span>, <span class="pl-s1">end</span>):
   <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">cur</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">start</span>
   <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">end</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">end</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__next__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">cur</span> <span class="pl-c1">&lt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">end</span>:
      <span class="pl-s1">val</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">cur</span>
      <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">cur</span> <span class="pl-c1">+=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>
      <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">val</span>
    <span class="pl-k">else</span>:
      <span class="pl-k">raise</span> <span class="pl-v">StopIteration</span>()

<span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">OurRange</span>:  <span class="pl-c"># iterable class</span>
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">end</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">end</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">end</span>

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__iter__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">iter</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">OurIter</span>(<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">end</span>)
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-s1">iter</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Notice the OurRange class, which is an iterable.  We construct it with the maximum value to iterate to, so it will iterate from [0,N).  The class implements an __iter__() method which is called to obtain an iterator into the iterable.  You can see that this method creates a new OurIter iterator, specifying the starting and ending range values.</p>
<p dir="auto">The OurIter class simply implements a __next__ method, just like any other iterator in python. This method obtains the next value if one is available,  then advances so the next call will return the next value in the range, and finally returns the value. If no more values are available in the range, the method raises a StopIteration exception, which is the way that Python indicates the iterator has reached the end of its iteration.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">"True Iterators" aka Generators</h4><a id="user-content-true-iterators-aka-generators" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: &quot;True Iterators&quot; aka Generators" href="#true-iterators-aka-generators"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">A "true iterator" is an iterator that is implemented by using a special type of function called a generator.</p>
<p dir="auto">A generator is essentially a closure that can be paused and resumed over time. Many languages have generators, but we'll use python to illustrate the concept since the syntax is pretty simple. But first let's start with pseudocode:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def foo(n):
  for i in range (1, n):
    print(f'i is {i}')
    pause
    print('woot!')

def main():
  p = create_pausable(func=foo, n=4)  # Line A
  print('CS')
  start(p)    # Line B
  print('is')
  resume(p)  # Line C
  print('cool!')
  resume(p)"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">foo</span>(<span class="pl-s1">n</span>):
  <span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">i</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-en">range</span> (<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-s1">n</span>):
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f'i is <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">i</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>'</span>)
    <span class="pl-s1">pause</span>
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'woot!'</span>)

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>():
  <span class="pl-s1">p</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">create_pausable</span>(<span class="pl-s1">func</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-s1">foo</span>, <span class="pl-s1">n</span><span class="pl-c1">=</span><span class="pl-c1">4</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># Line A</span>
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'CS'</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">start</span>(<span class="pl-s1">p</span>)    <span class="pl-c"># Line B</span>
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'is'</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">resume</span>(<span class="pl-s1">p</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># Line C</span>
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'cool!'</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">resume</span>(<span class="pl-s1">p</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Here's the general idea - remember the above is pseudocode:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Line A: You create a special closure (called a generator), which has one extra piece of data - an instruction pointer. The instruction pointer starts off on the first line of the function, and the function starts in a suspended state. It's not running at this point. We've just created the closure.</li>
<li>Line B: We wake up the generator/closure begin running it. It will run until it hits the pause command.  At that point, the instruction pointer is saved in the closure so we know where to continue running, and all changes made to the local variables in the closure are also retained. The generator returns to the next line of the main function and keeps running there. Later when we resume the generator, it continues running where it left off, with the same variables/values.</li>
<li>Line C: We resume the generator, and it continues running where it left off last time</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">So the above pseudocode would print:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="CS
i is 1
is
woot!
i is 2
cool!
woot!
i is 3"><pre class="notranslate"><code>CS
i is 1
is
woot!
i is 2
cool!
woot!
i is 3
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Now here's the real python syntax:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def foo(n):
  for i in range (1, n):
    print(f'i is {i}')
    yield
    print('woot!')

def main():
  p = foo(4)
  print('CS')
  next(p)
  print('is')
  next(p)
  print('cool!')
  next(p)"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">foo</span>(<span class="pl-s1">n</span>):
  <span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">i</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-en">range</span> (<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-s1">n</span>):
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f'i is <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">i</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>'</span>)
    <span class="pl-k">yield</span>
    <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'woot!'</span>)

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>():
  <span class="pl-s1">p</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">foo</span>(<span class="pl-c1">4</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'CS'</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">next</span>(<span class="pl-s1">p</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'is'</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">next</span>(<span class="pl-s1">p</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'cool!'</span>)
  <span class="pl-en">next</span>(<span class="pl-s1">p</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Here's what changed:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Instead of "pause" we use the keyword "yield" to pause the function</li>
<li>Insetad of calling create_pausable to create our closure, we just call the function and pass in the arguments, then store the return value in a variable. This does NOT run the function. It just creates the closure, and then returns an object reference to the closure. We then store the object reference to the closure inside our variable p. How does Python know not to run the function but just to create a closure? Because it has a "yield" command inside of it. This implicitly tells Python this is a generator function and not a traditional function, and that the first call should not run the function, but just create a closure</li>
<li>Instead of calling "start" to start the generator running, and "resume" to resume its execution, we just use next() on the closure that was returned during the initial call.</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">By the way, to use our earler iterable/iterator nomenclature, the generator function is an "iterable", and the closure that is returned when it's first called behaves like an iterator.</p>
<p dir="auto">Now let's see a more complex generator - it can not only yield its execution, but every time it yields it can return a value to the caller!</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def bar(a, b):
  while a &gt; b:
    yield a  # Line A
    a -= 1

f = bar(3, 0)
print('Eat prunes!')
t = next(f)  # Line B
print(t)
t = next(f)
print(t)
t = next(f)
print(t)
print(f'Explosive diarrhea!')"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">bar</span>(<span class="pl-s1">a</span>, <span class="pl-s1">b</span>):
  <span class="pl-k">while</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">b</span>:
    <span class="pl-k">yield</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span>  <span class="pl-c"># Line A</span>
    <span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">-=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>

<span class="pl-s1">f</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">bar</span>(<span class="pl-c1">3</span>, <span class="pl-c1">0</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Eat prunes!'</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">t</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">next</span>(<span class="pl-s1">f</span>)  <span class="pl-c"># Line B</span>
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">t</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">t</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">next</span>(<span class="pl-s1">f</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">t</span>)
<span class="pl-s1">t</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">next</span>(<span class="pl-s1">f</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">t</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f'Explosive diarrhea!'</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Notice that on Line A, the generator "yields a value". So not only does it pause itself, but it also returns a value at this time. Notice that on Line B, we wake up the generator and let it run until it yields a value. The yielded value is returned by next() and that value is stored in the t variable.</p>
<p dir="auto">This is a more idiomatic use of a generator – they're used to  "generate" a sequence of values that can be retrieved one at a time – the sequence might be finite, or infinite!</p>
<p dir="auto">Since a generator is an iterable object, and produces an iterator... You can use it like any other iterable object in loops! Another name for a generator function is a "true iterator."</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="def our_range(a, b):
  while a &gt; b:
    yield a
    a -= 1

print('Eat prunes!')
for t in our_range(3,0):
  print(t)
print(f'Explosive diarrhea!')"><pre><span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">our_range</span>(<span class="pl-s1">a</span>, <span class="pl-s1">b</span>):
  <span class="pl-k">while</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-s1">b</span>:
    <span class="pl-k">yield</span> <span class="pl-s1">a</span>
    <span class="pl-s1">a</span> <span class="pl-c1">-=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>

<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">'Eat prunes!'</span>)
<span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">t</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-en">our_range</span>(<span class="pl-c1">3</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>):
  <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s1">t</span>)
<span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f'Explosive diarrhea!'</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Here's a Javascript generator:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// JavaScript defines generators with a * character after the function name
gen = function*(n) {
  yield 'I';
  yield 'want';
  yield n;
  yield 'cookies';
};

g = gen(10);
while (true) {
  r = g.next();
  if (r.done) break;
  console.log(r.value);
}
 
for (word of gen(3)) {
  console.log(word);
}"><pre><span class="pl-c">// JavaScript defines generators with a * character after the function name</span>
<span class="pl-s1">gen</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-k">function</span><span class="pl-c1">*</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">n</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-k">yield</span> <span class="pl-s">'I'</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-k">yield</span> <span class="pl-s">'want'</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-k">yield</span> <span class="pl-s1">n</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-k">yield</span> <span class="pl-s">'cookies'</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-s1">g</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-en">gen</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">10</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-k">while</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">true</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-s1">r</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-s1">g</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">next</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-k">if</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">r</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">done</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-k">break</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
  <span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">r</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-c1">value</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span>
 
<span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">word</span> <span class="pl-k">of</span> <span class="pl-en">gen</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span> <span class="pl-kos">{</span>
  <span class="pl-smi">console</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">log</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">word</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
<span class="pl-kos">}</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">And here's one in Kotlin:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-kotlin notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// Kotlin generators care called &quot;sequences&quot;
fun vals(start: Int) = sequence {
  var i = start
  while (true) {
    yield(i)
    ++i
  }
}

fun main(args: Array&lt;String&gt;) {
  val iter = vals(42).iterator()
  var count = 3
  while (count-- &gt; 0) {
    var n = iter.next()
    println(n)
  } 
  
  for (n in vals(7).take(5))  
    println(n)     // 7, 8, 9, 10, 11
}"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Kotlin generators care called "sequences"</span>
<span class="pl-k">fun</span> <span class="pl-en">vals</span>(<span class="pl-smi">start</span><span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-c1">Int</span>) <span class="pl-k">=</span> sequence {
  <span class="pl-k">var</span> i <span class="pl-k">=</span> start
  <span class="pl-k">while</span> (<span class="pl-c1">true</span>) {
    <span class="pl-k">yield</span>(i)
    <span class="pl-k">++</span>i
  }
}

<span class="pl-k">fun</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>(<span class="pl-smi">args</span><span class="pl-k">:</span> <span class="pl-c1">Array</span>&lt;<span class="pl-en">String</span>&gt;) {
  <span class="pl-k">val</span> iter <span class="pl-k">=</span> vals(<span class="pl-c1">42</span>).iterator()
  <span class="pl-k">var</span> count <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">3</span>
  <span class="pl-k">while</span> (count<span class="pl-k">--</span> <span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span>) {
    <span class="pl-k">var</span> n <span class="pl-k">=</span> iter.next()
    <span class="pl-c1">println</span>(n)
  } 
  
  <span class="pl-k">for</span> (n <span class="pl-k">in</span> vals(<span class="pl-c1">7</span>).take(<span class="pl-c1">5</span>))  
    <span class="pl-c1">println</span>(n)     <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> 7, 8, 9, 10, 11</span>
}</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Analysis of Class-based Iterators and Generators</h4><a id="user-content-analysis-of-class-based-iterators-and-generators" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Analysis of Class-based Iterators and Generators" href="#analysis-of-class-based-iterators-and-generators"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Some things are easier to do with class-based iterators, and some things are easier to do with generators. But the two are isomorphic and functionally equivalent - anything we can do with a class we can do with a generator, and visa-versa.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">First-class function-based iteration</h3><a id="user-content-first-class-function-based-iteration" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: First-class function-based iteration" href="#first-class-function-based-iteration"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Alright, we'll end this lecture by looking at how some languages use first-class functions to do iteration. The syntax often looks something like this:</p>
<div class="snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="var fruits = ... // some list of fruits

fruits.forEach { f -&gt; println(&quot;$f&quot;) }"><pre class="notranslate"><code>var fruits = ... // some list of fruits

fruits.forEach { f -&gt; println("$f") }
</code></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Basically, the container (e.g., vector, list or set) contains a forEach() method, which accepts one parameter.  We pass in a { lambda } function to the forEeach method as this parameter.  The forEach method iterates  over each item in the iterable, and passes each item as the parameter to the lambda function (e.g., to the parameter f shown in the lambda above).</p>
<p dir="auto">Here are some examples:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-rust notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// Rust
(0..10).for_each(|elem| println!(&quot;{}&quot;, elem));

let items = vec![&quot;fee&quot;,&quot;fi&quot;,&quot;fo&quot;,&quot;fum&quot;];
items.iter().for_each(|elem| println!(&quot;{}&quot;, elem));"><pre><span class="pl-c">// Rust</span>
<span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span>..<span class="pl-c1">10</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">for_each</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span>|elem| <span class="pl-en">println</span><span class="pl-en">!</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"{}"</span>, elem<span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>

<span class="pl-k">let</span> items = <span class="pl-en">vec</span><span class="pl-en">!</span><span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-s">"fee"</span>,<span class="pl-s">"fi"</span>,<span class="pl-s">"fo"</span>,<span class="pl-s">"fum"</span><span class="pl-kos">]</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span>
items<span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">iter</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">for_each</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span>|elem| <span class="pl-en">println</span><span class="pl-en">!</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s">"{}"</span>, elem<span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">;</span></pre></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-ruby notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Ruby
(0..9).each do |elem| 
  print elem, &quot; &quot; 
end

items = [&quot;fee&quot;,&quot;fi&quot;,&quot;fo&quot;,&quot;fum&quot;]

items.each do |elem|
    print(elem,&quot;\n&quot;)
end"><pre><span class="pl-c"># Ruby</span>
<span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span>..<span class="pl-c1">9</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">each</span> <span class="pl-k">do</span> |<span class="pl-s1">elem</span>| 
  <span class="pl-en">print</span> <span class="pl-s1">elem</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span> <span class="pl-s">" "</span> 
<span class="pl-k">end</span>

<span class="pl-s1">items</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-kos">[</span><span class="pl-s">"fee"</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span><span class="pl-s">"fi"</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span><span class="pl-s">"fo"</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span><span class="pl-s">"fum"</span><span class="pl-kos">]</span>

<span class="pl-s1">items</span><span class="pl-kos">.</span><span class="pl-en">each</span> <span class="pl-k">do</span> |<span class="pl-s1">elem</span>|
    <span class="pl-en">print</span><span class="pl-kos">(</span><span class="pl-s1">elem</span><span class="pl-kos">,</span><span class="pl-s">"<span class="pl-cce">\n</span>"</span><span class="pl-kos">)</span>
<span class="pl-k">end</span></pre></div>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-kotlin notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="// Kotlin
(0..9).forEach({ elem -&gt; println(&quot;$elem&quot;) })

var items = arrayOf(&quot;fee&quot;,&quot;fi&quot;,&quot;fo&quot;,&quot;fum&quot;)
items.forEach({ elem -&gt; println(&quot;$elem&quot;) })"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Kotlin</span>
(<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-k">..</span><span class="pl-c1">9</span>).forEach({ elem <span class="pl-k">-&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">println</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-e">$elem</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) })

<span class="pl-k">var</span> items <span class="pl-k">=</span> arrayOf(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>fee<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>fi<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>fo<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>fum<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)
items.forEach({ elem <span class="pl-k">-&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">println</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-e">$elem</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) })</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">When we use this syntax, we're NOT using an iterator! Instead, we're passing a function as an argument to a forEach()/each() method that loops over the iterable's items!</p>
<p dir="auto">Let's build a forEach() method for our earlier Python container:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-python notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="class ListOfStrings:
  def __init__(self):
    self.array = []

  def add(self,val):
    self.array.append(val)

  def forEach(self, f):   # define our own for-each method
    for x in self.array:
      f(x)

yummy = ListOfStrings()
... # add items to yummy

def like(x):
 print(f'I like {x}'))

yummy.forEach(like)"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-v">ListOfStrings</span>:
  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">__init__</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">array</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> []

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">add</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>,<span class="pl-s1">val</span>):
    <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">array</span>.<span class="pl-en">append</span>(<span class="pl-s1">val</span>)

  <span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">forEach</span>(<span class="pl-s1">self</span>, <span class="pl-s1">f</span>):   <span class="pl-c"># define our own for-each method</span>
    <span class="pl-k">for</span> <span class="pl-s1">x</span> <span class="pl-c1">in</span> <span class="pl-s1">self</span>.<span class="pl-s1">array</span>:
      <span class="pl-en">f</span>(<span class="pl-s1">x</span>)

<span class="pl-s1">yummy</span> <span class="pl-c1">=</span> <span class="pl-v">ListOfStrings</span>()
... <span class="pl-c"># add items to yummy</span>

<span class="pl-k">def</span> <span class="pl-en">like</span>(<span class="pl-s1">x</span>):
 <span class="pl-en">print</span>(<span class="pl-s">f'I like <span class="pl-s1"><span class="pl-kos">{</span><span class="pl-s1">x</span><span class="pl-kos">}</span></span>'</span>))

<span class="pl-s1">yummy</span>.<span class="pl-en">forEach</span>(<span class="pl-s1">like</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Notice how the iterable object (a ListOfStrings) iterates over its own items, and calls the provided f(). This is essentially a map() operation like we saw in functional programming!</p>
